## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces, nonlinear damping, or time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal external driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic potential)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * v**2 (position-velocity coupling)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (polynomial potential with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium, indicating symmetric potential wells
- Even-power terms in x (x**2, x**4) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potentials or shifted equilibria
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (c<0) or injection (c>0) — linear damping/driving
- Products of x**2 and v (e.g., x**2*v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type self-oscillation
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces, leading to resonance phenomena
- Cubic position terms (x**3) with sign opposite to linear term indicate hardening (same sign as x) or softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Cross terms like x*v**2 arise from velocity-dependent potentials or relativistic corrections to oscillator dynamics

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
`-0.896123622766678*v - 1.29395390256765*x**3 - 1.29395390256765*x*(0.0943056786339846*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.29395390256765*x - 0.448061811383339*sin(v)`

Let me expand this:
- `-0.896123622766678*v`
- `-1.29395390256765*x**3`
- `-1.29395390256765*x*0.0943056786339846*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 - 1.29395390256765*x`
- `-1.29395390256765*x`
- `-0.448061811383339*sin(v)`

Combining the x terms:
`-1.29395390256765*x - 1.29395390256765*x = -2.5879078051353*x`

So GT = `-2.5879078051353*x - 1.29395390256765*x**3 - 0.896123622766678*v - 0.448061811383339*sin(v) - 0.12203844150498*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 * x`

The GT consists of these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `x**3`
3. `v` (linear)
4. `sin(v)`
5. `Abs(v)**(1/3) * x`

Key features:
- No `t` dependence
- Has `sin(v)` 
- Has `Abs(v)**(1/3) * x`
- No `v**3` term (the sin(v) approximation includes v**3 but sin(v) ≠ v - v³/6 exactly)
- No constant term

Now let me check each candidate. For a match, the candidate must be able to express exactly these 5 basis functions with appropriate constants. Candidates with `t` can match only if `t` terms can be zeroed out. Candidates with `v**3` cannot match because `sin(v)` cannot be expressed as a polynomial in `v`.

**Critical observation:** The GT contains `sin(v)`. Any candidate that lacks `sin(v)` (or an equivalent trigonometric function that can produce `sin(v)` via phase shift) cannot match, because `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomial and power-law functions.

Let me now scan all candidates:

- Candidates with `sin(...)`: **38, 39, 50** (these have `sin(c*x + c)`, not `sin(v)`)
- All other candidates use polynomial/power-law terms in `v` (like `v`, `v**3`, `v**c`, `log(...)`)

**None of the candidates contain `sin(v)`.**

Candidates 38, 39, 50 have `sin(c3*x + c4)`, which is a function of `x`, not `v`. Since `sin(v)` and `sin(x)` are different functions (different variables), these cannot match.

Let me verify candidates with `v**c` terms more carefully. Could `v**c` with some constant produce `sin(v)`? No - a power function `v**c` is a monomial, not a transcendental function. They are fundamentally different.

Could any candidate with `log(c*v + 1)` match `sin(v)`? No - `log` and `sin` are linearly independent.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT** because none contain `sin(v)` or any trigonometric function of `v`.
